  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer1234229690830863182">Light Yagami is an ace student with great prospects - and he's bored out of his mind. But all that changes when he finds the Death Note, a notebook dropped by a rogue Shinigami, a death god.   <span id="freeText1234229690830863182" style="display:none">Light Yagami is an ace student with great prospects - and he's bored out of his mind. But all that changes when he finds the Death Note, a notebook dropped by a rogue Shinigami, a death god. Any human whose name is written in the notebook dies, and now Light has vowed to use the power of the Death Note to rid the world of evil. But when criminals begin dropping dead, the authorities send the legendary detective L to track down the killer. With L hot on his heels, will Light lose sight of his noble goal... or his life?<br /><br />Boredom<br />Light tests the boundaries of the Death Note's powers as L and the police begin to close in. Luckily, Light's father is the head of the Japanese National Police Agency and leaves vital information about the case lying around the house. With access to his father's files, Light can keep one step ahead of the authorities. But who is the strange man following him, and how can Light guard against enemies whose names he doesn't know?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1234229690830863182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_134292881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134292881" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134292881?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134292881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2257924804641294765"><b>4 1/2 stars</b><br/>When I wrote in my review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/57891.Battle_Royale' title='Battle Royale by Koushun Takami' rel='nofollow noopener'>Battle Royale</a> that there were only two manga series I really enjoyed, it made me realise just how much in need of a review this was. I am not a manga fan, I know some people love it like crazy, but I've tried starting the most commonly loved - Naruto, InuYasha, Fullmetal Alchemist, etc. - and been left believing that I would never come to appreciate these graphic novels. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13615.Death_Note_Vol_1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Death Note</a> was a complete accident which I found one day whilst browsing youtube. I ra</span>
  <span id="freeText2257924804641294765" style="display:none"><b>4 1/2 stars</b><br />When I wrote in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/57891.Battle_Royale" title="Battle Royale by Koushun Takami" rel="nofollow noopener">Battle Royale</a> that there were only two manga series I really enjoyed, it made me realise just how much in need of a review this was. I am not a manga fan, I know some people love it like crazy, but I've tried starting the most commonly loved - Naruto, InuYasha, Fullmetal Alchemist, etc. - and been left believing that I would never come to appreciate these graphic novels. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13615.Death_Note_Vol_1" rel="nofollow noopener">Death Note</a> was a complete accident which I found one day whilst browsing youtube. I ran into the first episode and watched out of curiosity, then I watched the next and the next until I'd seen the whole thing and knew I had to read the novels too. <b>Both are brilliant</b>. The whole series has only one flaw for me and that's why I deducted half a star from the rating. I will talk about this issue later on.<br /><br />Just so you know, this is going to be a review of the series as a whole because I'm not going to review every single volume, but I promise to leave out any spoilers.<br /><br />Here goes: <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13615.Death_Note_Vol_1" rel="nofollow noopener">Death Note</a> is brilliant</b>. It's incredibly clever and will challenge your views on justice and power, but the challenges it puts your way are far from simple. I guarantee that you will change your mind multiple times during each volume; you will switch sides constantly; you will one minute think Light Yagami is evil and the next you'll think him a hero. This is a very complex moral story about right and wrong, about how power corrupts, and about what is a just punishment for the wicked.<br /><br />Light Yagami is an over-achieving student who is fed up with the world around him - day by day he hears the news report listing murders and rapes and other atrocities committed by human scum. When one day a Shinigami (Japanese death god) drops his death note into the human realm, Light Yagami picks it up and holds in his hands the power to kill people just by writing their names and picturing their faces whilst doing so. He starts out with the most noble intentions - rid the earth of the foulest criminals - but there's a price to pay for playing god. As people start to realise that somehow someone is murdering criminals and disregarding Japan's law methods, questions about justice begin to arise - <b>is the killer doing the world a favour, or is he showing a complete lack of respect for human rights?</b><br /><br />When more people begin to stand in Light's way, he is forced to write the names of more and more individuals - some criminals, some not. The power granted to him begins to change him, force him deeper into his obsession with this god-like role. All the while, Ohba maintains a brilliant pace and throws up many obstacles and challenges. This story will really appeal to people who want something to think about and are sick of reading novels with the same old pattern.<br /><br />On top of all this, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13615.Death_Note_Vol_1" rel="nofollow noopener">Death Note</a> has possibly my favourite detective of all time. When the Japanese police force realise that they are unqualified to catch the killer, they appeal to L Lawliet for help. Now, I don't want to say too much about L because I could spoil it, but he's intelligent, lovable, brilliant... I doubt you'll be able to resist loving L Lawliet. And this is one of the things I love most about the series: <b>there's no clear line between good and bad</b>. The novel pits Light and L against one another, they have very different ideas about justice and right and wrong, but the brilliance of it is that you can see it from both points of view, in a way you find yourself on both of their sides. <br /><br />So why did I knock off half a star? Because I dislike the way women are portrayed in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13615.Death_Note_Vol_1" rel="nofollow noopener">Death Note</a>. At the end of the day, this series was made to mainly appeal to young adult males. There's no heroine and very few main female characters appear throughout the whole thing. Also, the most central female character is Misa Amane and she is beautiful but useless. She is silly and fickle, and she is mostly regarded with contempt from the other characters. This would probably annoy me more if the rest of the story wasn't so excellent, but it is, it really is.<br /><br />You should read it. Or watch it. Each episode is only 20 minutes long, why not try out the first and see if it's something you could like: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CheI5Dse2jU">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CheI5D...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2257924804641294765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1144061285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1144061285" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144061285?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144061285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4784188739633044096">I don't read very much manga. But I picked the first few books of this series up on a whim, then quickly bought all the rest so I could finish the series. <br/><br/>Short version? I really enjoyed it. <br/><br/>Longer version: Here's some thoughts in no particular order.... <br/><br/>~ Great example of how you don't need a bunch of crazy fantastic things happening to make something a gripping piece of Speculative Fiction. In this series, you've got a notebook, and if someone writes your name in it, you die. It doesn't seem l</span>
  <span id="freeText4784188739633044096" style="display:none">I don't read very much manga. But I picked the first few books of this series up on a whim, then quickly bought all the rest so I could finish the series. <br /><br />Short version? I really enjoyed it. <br /><br />Longer version: Here's some thoughts in no particular order.... <br /><br />~ Great example of how you don't need a bunch of crazy fantastic things happening to make something a gripping piece of Speculative Fiction. In this series, you've got a notebook, and if someone writes your name in it, you die. It doesn't seem like that should be enough to carry twelve graphic novels worth of story, but it absolutely does. <br /><br />~ These books break a lot of my rules-of-thumb in terms of what makes a good story. The vast majority of the action is people thinking about things. That's a definite "no" in terms of storytelling, and I'd think it would be a double "no" in a visual medium like this. But it works. You can't argue with that. <br /><br />~ I think the series took a definite dip 2/3rds of the way through. It felt to me like the story reached a natural ending point, then just kept on bulling ahead, ignoring it. <br /><br />I've seen this happen before with a fair number of successful US comics (And a few series of novels). And while it's nice to see that this isn't not a problem unique to US publishing, I still have a severe distaste for stories that don't end properly. Doubly so if they feel like they're being infinitely extended just because the author won't let go, or because the publisher wants to keep selling more books. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4784188739633044096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3463065978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7066330591102726599"><i> <blockquote><b>“There is no heaven or hell. No matter what you do while you’re alive, everybody goes to the same place once you die. Death is Equal.” </b></blockquote>
<br/><br/> Shall we begin?* Ryuk laughs in background *<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596300005ra/29900545.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Before you read this , a little advice please watch the anime if you dont have time to read the manga. It's only 37 episodes , 20 min each , for free on YouTube with eng subs !<br/><br/>Assuming you have watched it because this review is going to be spoilery mess!!!<br/><br/>One more thing , if you think that death note is for teens obs</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7066330591102726599" style="display:none"><i> <blockquote><b>“There is no heaven or hell. No matter what you do while you’re alive, everybody goes to the same place once you die. Death is Equal.” </b></blockquote>
<br><br> Shall we begin?* Ryuk laughs in background *<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596300005ra/29900545.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Before you read this , a little advice please watch the anime if you dont have time to read the manga. It's only 37 episodes , 20 min each , for free on YouTube with eng subs !<br><br>Assuming you have watched it because this review is going to be spoilery mess!!!<br><br>One more thing , if you think that death note is for teens obsessed with idea of being smart and killing people to prove their worth please just get lost! I have spend enough time defending myself !<br><br> It is just outstanding and beyond words!! There is no Anime/Manga like Death Note and I can debate on this anyone.<br><br>The story is unique. A notebook falls from the sky, and the human who writes a name in it is capable of killing the individual pictured in his mind (I left out the details that you don't care about). This presents the readers with a highly debatable theme based on morals and justice. Yagami Light, who obtains this power to kill, utilizes it in hopes of creating a utopia in which he is god. Criminals, and only criminals, are to be punished in hopes of a perfect society.<b> Is this however, right? Is it right to kill individuals who have done wrong, and will do wrong again? Can they be reformed? Death Note presents the readers with questions such as these, questions which cannot be easily answers.</b><br><br> This series challenges the viewers morals and for that, it deserves highly.<br><br>Moving on characters, unpopular opinions and fan based theories :-<br><br><b> ✏L lawliet </b>:- he is my favourite character in the series and it's his intelligence , quirkiness and everything he stands for and not to forget his smile and his love for ice cream .<br><br>Bitch I cried when he died! Okay!<br><br><blockquote><b>Kira is childish and he hates losing... I am also childish and I hate to lose. That's how I know.” </b></blockquote>
<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596300005ra/29900546.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>✏Light*i don't give a fuck about anything*Yagami </b><br>:- my second fav character , and now here is a thing I love L like 55% and light like 45% and I can't decide whether I am team kira or team anti kira.<br>He is like my beyond imagination intelligent and smart but eventually he met his end, because it was necessary you see but if in some alternate world Light lives, I honestly don't have problem with it . Period ( don't fight me , I had enough discussion over this with my mum)<br><blockquote><b>"This world is rotten, and those who are making it rot deserve to die. Someone has to do it, so why not me?” </b></blockquote>
<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596300005ra/29900547.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now my next fav characters will be ryuk , mello, misa, near ( in that order)<br>I love mello soo much and I have great respect for near and people who say after L's death the series became boring and near wasn't that much intersting , I agree but it was necessary to introduce someone and near never said he is L , he used to call himself L's successor always !!!!<br><br><b> Unpopular opinion :- I like Misa </b> <br>▪She is smart than people think.<br>▪ She brushes off torture like no one else.<br>▪ Her love for Light , knows no command.<br>▪She adds color and humor to manga( bet if you didn't laughed at her silliness)<br>▪And not to forget her fashion sense!<br><br>Now I am believer of the most famous death note fan theory of Light becoming shinigami at the end( if you too let me know)<br><br>In the end acc to me, death note is one of the most iconic manga/anime I have ever read/watched like there is nothing like this and i recommend everyone to watch/read it once in their lifetime .<br><br>It will make you question things you never would have brainstormed . Because low-key we all know we would have done the exact same thing when we would have got the death note.<br><br><blockquote>
<b>"In the end, there is no greater motivation than revenge.”</b><br>
</blockquote>
<br>Thank you!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595857494ra/29865154.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></i></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1190946474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2971163000131835950">Death Note vol. 1 shows well drawn graphics, an anti-hero as main character that surprises/shocks, a *monster* that becomes actually…endearing, controversial themes that will provoke raw emotions along with deep thoughts and a writing and dialogs that make the characters look real and three dimensional without a doubt.<br/><br/>I think the plot could have been more developed, though. The Shinigami world better seen and much more exploited and maybe even contain a notable amount of interesting descriptions</span>
  <span id="freeText2971163000131835950" style="display:none">Death Note vol. 1 shows well drawn graphics, an anti-hero as main character that surprises/shocks, a *monster* that becomes actually…endearing, controversial themes that will provoke raw emotions along with deep thoughts and a writing and dialogs that make the characters look real and three dimensional without a doubt.<br><br>I think the plot could have been more developed, though. The Shinigami world better seen and much more exploited and maybe even contain a notable amount of interesting descriptions for the creatures inside it, because it lacked of it. Badly.<br><br>Nonetheless, one of the most original manga volumes I’ve had the chance to read in months!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423094250i/13587143._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<div id="review_8535950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8535950" />
    <a title="Seth T." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/160319-seth-t"><img alt="Seth T." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251915636p2/160319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8535950?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth T." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth T." href="/user/show/160319-seth-t">Seth T.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">pretty much anyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/160319-seth-t?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8535950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8542438530371089986">Over the past three weeks I've been burning through one of the most exciting reads I've come across in a while. <i>Death Note</i> is a seat-edged battle of wits that left me exhausted by the end. Heck, I was exhausted by the halfway mark.<br/><br/>Let me start over. <i>Death Note</i> is a Japanese comic that tells it's story over the course of twelve volumes (on display now at your local Borders). If what I'm about to say sounds good but you don't feel like spending the eight dollars per volume, head to your local libr</span>
  <span id="freeText8542438530371089986" style="display:none">Over the past three weeks I've been burning through one of the most exciting reads I've come across in a while. <i>Death Note</i> is a seat-edged battle of wits that left me exhausted by the end. Heck, I was exhausted by the halfway mark.<br /><br />Let me start over. <i>Death Note</i> is a Japanese comic that tells it's story over the course of twelve volumes (on display now at your local Borders). If what I'm about to say sounds good but you don't feel like spending the eight dollars per volume, head to your local library - they almost certainly carry the books in the Young Adults section. In any case, it's worth your time. Here's why.<br /><br />The story begins when Ryuk, a death god (known in the story's mythology as <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shinigami/" rel="nofollow noopener">shinigami</a>), drops a death note into the human world in order to alleviate the boredom that oppresses his everlasting life. A death note is a special notebook possessed by shinigami that allow them to take the lives of humans whose names they write into the notebook. Ryuk's dropped notebook "happens" to fall into the path of Japan's top high school student, son of the chief of police, and all around genius, Light Yagami.<br /><br />After a couple tests of the book's authenticity and the boundaries of some of its rules (e.g., one must visualize the face of the person whose name he is writing for that person to die), Light decides that he will forge a new world, a utopia in which all criminals (those would would take advantage of the weakness of others) simply die. Rather quickly, the police around the world begin taking notice of the staggering number of criminals who have suddenly dropped dead of heart attacks. Suspecting foul play, they want to find the perpetrator because law-and-order and vigilantism have never been the best bed-fellows. And it doesn't help that Light has gained a popular following amongst the masses who dub him Kira (which sounds remarkably similar to the Japanese pronunciation of the English word, "killer"). So the authorities enlist the assistance of the world's greatest detective (an anonymous man known only as L) and he quickly narrows the range of suspects dramatically, instigating a pulse-pounding game of of cat-and-mouse between the figures - L vs. Kira.<br /><br />Initially, as exciting as the first couple volumes were, I had a hard time seeing how the story could sustain itself across twelve volumes. The key to Death Note's happy success is the absence of anything really resembling a status quo. The story and its elements are continually in flux. If things remained simple, I could see the book resolving in four or five volumes but everything is constantly moving, constantly changing. It was a fantastic read.<br /><br />And smart. The fact that you're reading about these very intelligent characters who think things through to incredible lengths only adds to the excitement. There were moments of revelation and counter-revelation that simply blew my mind. And then there are moments when you think the jig is up for one or more of the characters and then a flashback will reveal the would-be victims plan from the start and you get to see tables turn and over turn as these characters fight for their lives.<br /><br />And even after that, the moral question that is explored by the book's author and artist really goes to lengths to get the reader thinking about means and ends and it's not at all clear who one should root for. It helps that Light, despite having an ego that won't quit, is entirely unselfish in his motivation. <i>Death Note</i> is almost a distillation of an important moral question.<br /><br />In short, I highly recommend this series to just about anyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8542438530371089986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16569627148951146926" style="display:none">This was my very FIRST expedition into magna and <b>ahhh I so loved it!!</b> I mean, once I started reading the book in the right direction. Ahem. And I only got mixed up like 859 while reading it...BUT HEY. I'M SURE I'LL GET BETTER WITH TIME. I'm also <i>really</i> annoyed I only got the first book from the library because a) cliffhanger and b) I WANNA KNOW WHAT HAPPENS NEXT AND I ONLY GO TO THE LIBRARY ON THURSDAYS. *hyperventilates*<br /><br />Least to say, I obviously am a fan.<br /><br /><b>I loved the story!</b> Like the mixture of death gods and an overachieving super smart highschooler. Duuuuude, Light was a GENIUS. I mean, apart from the part where he was really stupid and has this "I wanna be god" complex. But he was really smart and laid detailed traps and tricked the police and I'm just impressed. <b>I love the trope of criminals vs masterminds.</b><br /><br />But his name is <i>Light?</i>??? Ah-huh.<br /><br /><b>I'm also 10000% sure this is more of an anti-hero story.</b> I mean, Light is killing people in order to make a utopia. BUT HE'S STILL KILLING THEM. THE DUDE IS MESSED UP.<br /><br />Also did I mention I was addicted and read the whole thing in one sitting? THERE'S THAT.<br /><br />I also <b>really liked the art</b>. (Although I'm a bit confused as to the dude who's name starts with W [I seriously can't remember] and if he's working for L or <i>is</i> L or...what. Hrughugh?) And I think Light was kinda adorable. Also the death god creature/monster, Ryuk? HE WAS FUNNY SOMETIMES. Between being kind of creepy and all that. Ahem.<br /><br /><b>Okay, so I'm sold. I want to read more magna!</b> (I also fully admit this is "research" for my writing because I'm setting a book in Japan. ahem. Totally legit.) I love paranormals and mysteries and I LOVE battle-of-wits and antiheroes. sO. MUCH. WIN. HERE.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2435051628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15408912301438042990"><b>Death Note is one of the most amazing series ever with amazing characters, themes of religion and what justice is and all of this wrapped up in an exhilarating cat and mouse game between two geniuses.</b><br/><br/>It was amazing to watch these two geniuses try to outsmart one another through their constant, expert use of lying and manipulation. I was astonished by how quick the two were to constantly outsmart the other’s fool proof plans.<br/><br/>L was definitely my favourite of the two, with his quirky characteristic</span>
  <span id="freeText15408912301438042990" style="display:none"><b>Death Note is one of the most amazing series ever with amazing characters, themes of religion and what justice is and all of this wrapped up in an exhilarating cat and mouse game between two geniuses.</b><br><br>It was amazing to watch these two geniuses try to outsmart one another through their constant, expert use of lying and manipulation. I was astonished by how quick the two were to constantly outsmart the other’s fool proof plans.<br><br>L was definitely my favourite of the two, with his quirky characteristics and his amazing levels of deduction blending seamlessly. It was a delight to watch him pose a serious challenge to Light, through his amazing abilities of manipulation and deduction skills, in ways that no else could.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I love L. I would die for him. I would give anything for him to come back <b>But</b> i see a lot of people complaining about how the series lost its charm after L's death. Yes i was shattered after that but <b>Near</b> was important to the series. Without Near (who represents L's calculating side) Light would never have fallen. He is the one who constantly challenges Light's beliefs. Even the sentence he first says to Light throws him off guard. He is the one who makes Light question (in the scene where they throw the money from the aeroplane) that his followers have a lack of determination to follow Kira by proving how easily distracted they are. In the end Light and L were grown ups. They would never and could never grasp the real evil all along. <b>the Death Note.</b> But Near being a child grasped this reality. And that is the brilliance of this series. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>In comparison, Light is also thrilling and mysterious. He is almost, if not just as smart as L but his Death Note gives him a considerable edge. And, although Light is setting out to make a better world, his way of doing so and one of his main motivations raise serious questions about his morality.<br><br><b>The Philosophy of Death Note : What Is Justice?</b><br>Even the series doesn't answer this question. Throughout the whole series we see characeters with their individual POV's on what Justice is. We see Light, L, Near, Mello and in the end we are forced to admit once again that <b>
  <i>there are no good or bad people in this world. We live in a world where people are morally grey. Some darker than others, others not so much. But still the good and bad together are what constitutes us.</i>
</b> <br><br>A total must read/must watch for everyone!<br><br><b>
  <u>This is still the one of most iconic scenes in cinematic/manga history.</u>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595148184ra/29840058.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595148184ra/29840059.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595148184ra/29840060.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595148184ra/29840061.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595148184ra/29840062.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595148184ra/29840063.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>And this is still one of the saddest scenes in manga/cinematic history.</u>
</b> <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[

<div id="review_3620799784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3620799784" />
    <a title="Lauren Lanz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82987361-lauren-lanz"><img alt="Lauren Lanz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586150400p2/82987361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3620799784?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Lanz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Lanz" href="/user/show/82987361-lauren-lanz">Lauren Lanz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=author-of-colour">author-of-colour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3620799784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14794866544792425719"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Start looking around you... and all you see are people the world would be better off without.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Wow. It's no wonder <i>Death Note</i> is such a wildly popular manga. I loved everything about this first volume! The characters and prose were unlike anything I’ve read before.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>~★~ What is this book about? ~★~</u>
</b><br/><br/>When Ryuk -a god of death- drops his notebook, Light Yagami is the one to find it. The notebook is titled <i>Death Note</i>, and guarantees the death of anyone whose name is written in it. Ryuk </span>
  <span id="freeText14794866544792425719" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Start looking around you... and all you see are people the world would be better off without.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Wow. It's no wonder <i>Death Note</i> is such a wildly popular manga. I loved everything about this first volume! The characters and prose were unlike anything I’ve read before.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>~★~ What is this book about? ~★~</u>
</b><br /><br />When Ryuk -a god of death- drops his notebook, Light Yagami is the one to find it. The notebook is titled <i>Death Note</i>, and guarantees the death of anyone whose name is written in it. Ryuk and Light become unlikely acquaintances, and embark on a mission to eliminate criminals using the book. The sudden sequence of deaths happening amongst prisoners raises alarm amongst the authority, putting Light in more danger than he first anticipated.<br /><br />~★~<br /><br />The dynamic between a high school student and a god of death was not one I expected to pore over, but alas, here we are. Light and Ryuk are such bizarre characters, it was nearly impossible not to love them. Light’s nonchalance towards meeting an outwardly terrifying creature was pretty hilarious… and <i>Ryuk</i>, oh Ryuk. This duo is going to be a problem for me in all the best ways, I know it.<br /><br />The plot of <i>Death Note</i> is so intriguing, I flew through this volume in no time. I loved seeing Light and L attempt to discover each other's identity with Ryuk monitoring their proceedings. It’s a mystery as to what’ll happen next, but I can’t wait to find out.<br /><br />I’m pretty sure <i>Death Note</i> is also the most read manga on Goodreads, and it’s evident as to why. This is a tale that even people who’ve never read manga before will love, and that in itself is a great feat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14794866544792425719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1997305226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer313887541516114263">My first toe dip into the world of Manga, this was enjoyable and packed full of surprises and colourful characters. <br/><br/>What would you do if you had the ability to kill anyone in the world just by writing their name and picturing their face, in a book? That's the situation Light finds himself in when he comes across the Deathnote. Soon he finds himself persued by the police, and the mysterious 'L', as he tries to complete his dream of creating a utopia free of violence by killing the worlds criminal</span>
  <span id="freeText313887541516114263" style="display:none">My first toe dip into the world of Manga, this was enjoyable and packed full of surprises and colourful characters. <br /><br />What would you do if you had the ability to kill anyone in the world just by writing their name and picturing their face, in a book? That's the situation Light finds himself in when he comes across the Deathnote. Soon he finds himself persued by the police, and the mysterious 'L', as he tries to complete his dream of creating a utopia free of violence by killing the worlds criminals. <br /><br />I suppose the overriding theme here is does anyone have the right to take another's life, even if that life has done nothing but evil? Choice, surely must always play a part. Light is arrogant with his power, and lets it go to his head big time. He thinks he can outdo the worlds police, that he's smarter than everyone he meets. Honestly, he's not a nice guy. Which comes as a surprise, because from the start I though he was going to be the protagonist. The antihero. He's anything but. Ryuk by comparison, the shinigami who owns the Deathbook is a great character. He's funny, often feigning melancholy at his life before coming to earth, and appearing interested yet also completely nonplussed at what Light is doing. <br /><br />The plot is also really interesting. Far from being straightforward, it had plenty of twists and surprises to further the plot and make it exciting. I'm actually amazed that such a complex story can be told in so few words. <br /><br />My only criticism is the lack of any female presence through this volume. We see Light's mother, sister and a random girl who takes on a 'date'. All the main characters are men. And most of the secondary cast too. A bit of female presence would have been welcome. </span>
  <a data-text-id="313887541516114263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3757106962955188940"><b>This is more of my opinion on the whole series instead of the first volume.</b><br/><br/>Death note is a highly addictive read. I would say it’s the best manga I’ve ever read. It’s one of those stories which leaves you desperate for the ending, but at the same time upset because it all ended. Everything in Death note was planned out perfectly and it was very fast-paced so I was never fed up.<br/><br/>However, I do have a problem with the protagonist.   <span id="freeText3757106962955188940" style="display:none"><b>This is more of my opinion on the whole series instead of the first volume.</b><br /><br />Death note is a highly addictive read. I would say it’s the best manga I’ve ever read. It’s one of those stories which leaves you desperate for the ending, but at the same time upset because it all ended. Everything in Death note was planned out perfectly and it was very fast-paced so I was never fed up.<br /><br />However, I do have a problem with the protagonist. Light’s character was never developed well. He suddenly just turns evil after gaining the notebook. He appeared like a perfectly normal high-schooler, but he becomes a cold-blooded killer in matter of days. I don’t buy it. There must be some progression. I wanted to see him regret his actions slightly at first before turning fully evil.<br /><br />Besides that, it’s fantastic!<br /></span>

<div id="review_1638796051" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638796051?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=artistic-absorption">artistic-absorption</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638796051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10600670570289710693">My first graphic novel and manga experience was definitely a good one and I might already be hooked!<br/><br/>I didn't know how I would get on with the format but I found myself just as immersed in the story, after a few pages, as I would an ordinary novel. This managed to pack in so much in such little text and I was consistently guessing where the plot would take me next. It also managed to transgress into so many genres that I find it hard that there would be a reader who would not like this!<br/><br/>The story </span>
  <span id="freeText10600670570289710693" style="display:none">My first graphic novel and manga experience was definitely a good one and I might already be hooked!<br /><br />I didn't know how I would get on with the format but I found myself just as immersed in the story, after a few pages, as I would an ordinary novel. This managed to pack in so much in such little text and I was consistently guessing where the plot would take me next. It also managed to transgress into so many genres that I find it hard that there would be a reader who would not like this!<br /><br />The story follows high school super brain, Light, after he acquires a magical notebook that has fallen to earth. This is, of course, the Death Note, and each person written in the pages will find themselves deceased before the minute is out. Light manages to become the perfect anti-villain and his wit, super smart tactics and willingness to do good with his new evil power aligned me to his immoral cause. <br /><br />The artwork was simplistic in colour and design and yet its varied format and sizing kept each page feeling fresh and pleasing to the eye. Takeshi Obata is a one seriously good artist and his skill really helped to bring this story to life. I can't wait to see more of his brilliant work and continue on with Tsugumi Ohba's complex and compelling story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10600670570289710693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17716555752542329035">Every one on social media was getting freak about Death Note.   <span id="freeText17716555752542329035" style="display:none">Every one on social media was getting freak about Death Note. I just couldn't understand why. <br /><br />Until the day, after whole two years dive of this ignorance, I finally got to read the manga that totally blowen my mind, that got me hooked since the first lines. <br /><br />To tell you the truth, I never paid attention to it's title. Never cared, not at all. <br /><br />So when I read this manga, I was surely to stay amazed until and unless I reached to the end. <br /><br />All pieces started to connect. The truth was before me, the facts were before me.<br /><br />I tried to talk about it with some of my friends, they won't listen and won't read this manga. <br /><br />So I had to categorize them personally in my mind to a 'Never to suggest anything' list. Ever.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2074466092394080270">I think if a Shinigami gave you a death note – oh, I should say a Shinigami is a like god or spirit who controls the way HUMANS (meaning YOU) DIE (meaning DIE!) and also WHEN just by writing it down, and also this death NOTE is not a note, it’s a NOTEBOOK, just to be crystal clear – but anyway, why this becomes an issue is that this particular shinagami is really bored in the realm where he & his other death gods live – they always live in a REALM, have you noticed, never in a house or an apartm</span>
  <span id="freeText2074466092394080270" style="display:none">I think if a Shinigami gave you a death note – oh, I should say a Shinigami is a like god or spirit who controls the way HUMANS (meaning YOU) DIE (meaning DIE!) and also WHEN just by writing it down, and also this death NOTE is not a note, it’s a NOTEBOOK, just to be crystal clear – but anyway, why this becomes an issue is that this particular shinagami is really bored in the realm where he &amp; his other death gods live – they always live in a REALM, have you noticed, never in a house or an apartment, always a realm – anyway, it turns out in the death god realm there’s nothing much to do, they get really bored writing down name after name with stroke or general organ failure or rabies or giraffe attack next to them, these shinagami don’t have much initiative otherwise they could of I dunno got a franchise to make a death realm Disneyland or play crazy golf or I don’t know what people do for entertainment, lot of the people I know just watch football, so maybe they could get Sky up there and follow the English Premier League, and see how Manchester United gets on under Ole Gunnar Solskjær, whatever, the clue is in the title of this first volume here BOREDOM, so because of that this particular shinagami leaves a death note (= noteBOOK) for this 17 year old kid to find and then he has the power to make anyone dead and that’s what you call a responsibility, I wouldn’t want that.<br /><br />But I wouldn’t mind if a lower-ranking Shinigami from a lower REALM left me a SICK NOTE so I could make anyone really ill, that would be great, a lot of politicians I could name would be rolling around on Christmas Day after the turkey &amp; not in a good way.<br /><br />So is this 17 year old kid’s plan to make the world a better place by killing lots of people ethically sound or not? This is the big issue. Omelets, eggs, eggs, omelets. If Pol Pot was asked he would have said YES. Likewise Stalin. But if you asked Princess Diana or Walt Disney they would have said NO. Hmm, Stalin, Princess Diana, Pol Pot, Walt Disney. It’s above my pay grade.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2135806129" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15361296995806071051">Update 14.01.18 <br/>I’ve got to remove my rating from here. I wasn’t a fan of this manga but I’ve come to realize that I might just not be a fan of manga as a genre, period. HOWEVER, having just finished the entirety of death note in the form of an anime, I’d like to come to my knees and admit that I was WRONG. like, seriously. I’m so shook. <br/><br/><br/>This was just. weird. Also, no offense, but the graphics were quite ugly. Should I even bother with the next volume? Does it get any better? Idk, man.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KcuGak39UsVdFInd3sWvvmGdenlR5kuYo74FwgS2DlUT7e+49qObrfo/PbwpMKVht8KdsZ9rxf/4wENzyfX8zw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7Qy4YPgfQnbjkMgArIrVCI5Vp8uviQfdrGBvES+YO/bXKtGyQ0GLHkS7fGFbf9/XWApAA2EEibr3Himg4tvJbA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5502079.Tsugumi_Ohba">About Tsugumi Ohba</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5502079.Tsugumi_Ohba"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1476730775p3/5502079.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5502079.Tsugumi_Ohba">Tsugumi Ohba
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,032
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer346178355425222016">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______' title='大場 つぐみ' rel='nofollow noopener'>大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br/><br/>There is spe</span>
  <span id="freeText346178355425222016" style="display:none">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______" title="大場 つぐみ" rel="nofollow noopener">大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br /><br />There is speculation that Tsugumi Ōba is a pen name and that he is really Hiroshi Gamō. Pointing out that in Bakuman the main character's uncle was a one-hit wonder manga artist who worked on a gag super hero manga, very similar to Gamō and Tottemo! Luckyman in all aspects. Also that the storyboards drawn by Ōba greatly resemble Tottemo! Luckyman in style.</span>

    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
